  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e01c4062-e427-4cd9-9310-4dbe25e1747d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10027751718565745098"><b>
  <u>Goosebumpy alright!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>This is the first book of the original book series of “Goosebumps”</i><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>CREEPY GOOD BOOK</u>
</b><br/><br/>Obviously I wasn’t expecting a scary bloody tale, since this is <i>Goosebumps</i>, not H.P. Lovecraft, but I am glad to say that the book is quite well written, with an engaging narrative and a kinda of “cliffhanger” or “shocking last line” on each chapter making you to keep reading.<br/><br/>I found ingenious that the main character (and narrator of the story) is a teenage girl, due this is the first boo</span>
  <span id="freeText10027751718565745098" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Goosebumpy alright!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>This is the first book of the original book series of “Goosebumps”</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>CREEPY GOOD BOOK</u>
</b><br /><br />Obviously I wasn’t expecting a scary bloody tale, since this is <i>Goosebumps</i>, not H.P. Lovecraft, but I am glad to say that the book is quite well written, with an engaging narrative and a kinda of “cliffhanger” or “shocking last line” on each chapter making you to keep reading.<br /><br />I found ingenious that the main character (and narrator of the story) is a teenage girl, due this is the first book of a series (that eventually became so popular and bestseller) having young audience as main targets, so the boys will pick the book since it’s terror, and the girls will pick the book since a girl is the main characters (without messing the topic with clichés of “women read romance”, “men read terror”, since I know for sure that it’s not the case) but as a business decision for a key first book in a series in this kind of genre and target audiences, I thought that it was well chosen.<br /><br />It was a book quick to read and I enjoyed a lot, it’s not something that it will give you nightmares but certainly it will give you…<br /><br />…goosebumps!<br /><br />And at the end, that’s the whole purpose of this series.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>WELCOME TO DARK FALLS</u>
</b><br /><br />You don’t have to be a rocket scientist to know that any town named “Dark Falls” isn’t a good place to go to live, but…<br /><br />…hey! If our heroes wouldn’t go there, we wouldn’t have a story to read, right?<br /><br /><u>Meet The Benson Family:</u> Dad, Mom, Amanda (the main character) (12 years old) and Josh (11 years old) along with their dog Petey (I guess they were huge fans of <i>The Little Rascals</i>).<br />They got a letter explaining that certain distant relative (that they never heard before (aaaha!) died and he left them his old house as inheritance.<br /><br />Of course, the house is on Dark Falls, and you can bet that the dang house has two Windows at front just like the Amityville House!!!<br /><br />But who cares? Free house!<br /><br />So, everybody packin’ folks! Since Dark Falls, here we go!<br /><br />Soon enough Amanda starting to notice here and there, strange happenings.<br /><br />Yep. Free house. Aha.<br /><br />But, don’t be so harsh on them! As I say, if they wouldn’t decided to live in that creepy house, we wouldn’t have this book to read.<br /><br />Thanks Benson Family!<br /><br />Good luck and I hope seeing you…<br /><br />…alive…<br /><br />…again…<br /><br />Free house. Dang!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10027751718565745098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1144649281" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144649281" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144649281?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590453653" href="/book/show/1194302.Welcome_to_Dead_House">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144649281" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1934866011970453296"><b>THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS.</b> <br/>From graphic descriptions of a family gnawing on moldy plates of human bones to a small town conspiring to murder the new family that has just moved into the creepiest house on the block, <i>Welcome to Dead House</i> easily could work as a standalone novel despite originally being marketed for children under the iconic and popular <i>Goosebumps</i> series. This bit of gothic supernatural horror is extremely dark and after backlash and censorship in the 1990's from horrified pare</span>
  <span id="freeText1934866011970453296" style="display:none"><b>THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS.</b> <br>From graphic descriptions of a family gnawing on moldy plates of human bones to a small town conspiring to murder the new family that has just moved into the creepiest house on the block, <i>Welcome to Dead House</i> easily could work as a standalone novel despite originally being marketed for children under the iconic and popular <i>Goosebumps</i> series. This bit of gothic supernatural horror is extremely dark and after backlash and censorship in the 1990's from horrified parents and teachers, R.L. Stine understandably toned down the content of his series in future installments to make them more comedic and less unsettling and sad. That being said, I think something was really lost when he did this, because <i>Welcome to Dead House</i> was one of the only books I can remember reading as a kid that was classified as horror but dealt with tragedy, family dysfunction and the overwhelming emotions and common fears associated with moving. He addressed these things both metaphorically and literally, and the book, unlike many other <i>Goosebumps</i> novels, doesn't try to avoid more serious themes, but instead dives into them with a surprising amount of depth and complexity for a book targeted towards twelve-year-olds.<br><br>I'll concede I was a much bigger fan of the TV film adaptation produced in 1997 and filmed on Toronto's industrial Unwin Avenue. I think the film did a better job at the scary factor with the usage of decrepit scenery, unsettling soundtrack and had the devastating chemical factory accident as more of a central plot device. I'd actually be surprised if there weren't a few <i>adults</i> not at least mildly creeped out by the film version (you have to watch it in the dark to get the full effect), created by the talented William Fruet who also brought us the 1980 horror film <i>Funeral Home</i>. The film also addressed economic depression in industrial towns in a way that seems much more appropriate for adults, with talk of people being fired from their jobs and a newspaper discussing an accident in the town's main employer, Dark Falls Chemical, an explosion which killed most of the workers and left the rest of the townspeople isolated and frustrated. The book vaguely touches on this but not in the same manner. The book, however, is still arguably the best children's horror story I've ever read. In it we have Amanda Benson, a girl who finds herself and her typical all-American family moving to a town that is anything but. Dark Falls is odd. More than odd. The sunlight is virtually non-existent, the townsfolk are asocial and rarely seen and everything seems abandoned. The other children living in town seem either very depressed or very menacing. We also have a real-estate agent, Compton Dawes, who seems to have no shortage of excuses for why the house looks "old and gross" or why the neighbourhood is so quiet. Amanda herself doesn't cope well with the move, having to leave a beloved friend behind in a very harrowing, tearful goodbye, and upon arriving in Dark Falls she begins to see things. As is often the case, her parents and brother begin to think she's troubled, chalking up her visions of dead people to be related to her anger over the move. Meanwhile dysfunction ensues within the family itself including Josh Benson running away from "home", the parents fighting over petty things like the crispiness of a piece of bacon and the family dog going missing. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532510083i/26025463._SX540_.png" height="427" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Things eventually take a turn for the downright brutal and shocking, including Mr. Dawes having his head beaten inward with a large halogen flashlight, a boy being melted apart to the point where his eyes pour out from his skull, the dog being killed and eaten by the townsfolk, descriptions of an unnamed "yellow gas" from the factory floating over Dark Falls and killing off all the residents of the town (luckily Stine spared his readers from knowing exactly <i>how</i> the gas worked, because <i>wow</i>) and a teenage girl named Karen actually <i>thanking</i> Amanda for killing her. I can see why there was a backlash against children reading this story. That being said at the time of its publication and to this day, it took the "haunted house" trope and used it to sympathize with a plight that most kids have to face at least once in their childhood. Moving is difficult, whether you see it as an adventurous new start or a cut-off from your friends and school. With moving from one place to another often comes the feeling that nobody understands you, that the people in your new town are weird or rude or different, and that everybody is out to get you, that you can't trust anyone. <i>Welcome to Dead House</i> creates the perfect metaphor for this, where everybody really <i>is</i> out to get you and you can't trust anyone, because they're all secretly conspiring to murder your family as a cruel means of survival.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1934866011970453296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299178566" />
    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299178566?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590453653" href="/book/show/1194302.Welcome_to_Dead_House">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299178566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12742786625312940783"><br/><br/>When it comes to horror movies I like them the same way I like my pizza- extra cheesy. However, the same cannot be said of my horror books. <br/><br/>Back when I was a <s>young lady</s> little turd, my favorite place in the world was a tiny library in an old fashioned town called Henderson. My aunt lived up the road, and when I say up, I mean it literally. Once I had a bag full of books I had to lug them up a hill that felt like it would never end. My siblings and I spent a lot of time there in the summers becau</span>
  <span id="freeText12742786625312940783" style="display:none"><br /><br />When it comes to horror movies I like them the same way I like my pizza- extra cheesy. However, the same cannot be said of my horror books. <br /><br />Back when I was a <s>young lady</s> little turd, my favorite place in the world was a tiny library in an old fashioned town called Henderson. My aunt lived up the road, and when I say up, I mean it literally. Once I had a bag full of books I had to lug them up a hill that felt like it would never end. My siblings and I spent a lot of time there in the summers because my mother was the manager of a convenient store right across the street from the library. My aunt’s house was also conveniently located in front of a playground and was surrounded by kids I went to school with. <br /><br />There was one summer in particular where I discovered the wonderful stories of R.L. Stine. I saw the covers with the bumped up letters and scary images and knew I had to have them all. And so my love of the macabre was born. <br /><br />While the neighborhood kids all played outside on the playground or at summer recreation or spent their day running under the hose, I could be found with my nose in a book. This is not to say, however, that I didn’t horse around when the time was right. There was horsing around aplenty. But, what I remember most is sitting under a tree, behind the garage, on my aunt’s fence, or holed up in the little tube at the playground reading as fast as my eyes would let me. I think I read every issue of Goosebumps available in that summer. <br /><br />And it is <i>that</i> summer that I remember most fondly.<br /><br />After losing my father to cancer about a year and a half ago, I have been on a bit of a quest. I’ve been trying to relive my youth in an attempt to rediscover myself; redefine myself in light of the overwhelming realities I’ve had to face.<br /><br />Reading Goosebumps was just one item on a list of several meant to help me through this journey. And oh! What a treat this truly was. I was immediately taken back to those summer days that felt endless. It was as if I had stepped into a time machine. I found myself laughing like a child again; my youth restored. I was able to find what had fascinated me so much as a kid again and that was an experience all in its own. <br /><br />The book itself is 100% a cheese-fest. I refuse to sugar coat it. The writing caused me to roll my eyes through most of it, the storyline so obvious and the characters…well they were cookie-cutouts at best. But, I can’t completely throw this book under the bus. The memories it brought up, the feeling I had in my soul, the laughter that poured out of me at the silliness of it all- those things are worth more than any money in the world. <br /><br /> I look forward to reading more of these and hope that they still bring me the joy that they once did- even if it comes in a different form.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12742786625312940783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17717318063240893741">There's something off about the old house Amanda's dad inherited from a deceased uncle he's never heard of. <br/><br/><i>A cold breeze made me shiver. It was actually a beautiful, hot summer day. But the closer we got to the house, the colder I felt</i>. <br/><br/><i>Welcome to Dead House</i> offers a satisfying blend of camp and creepiness: <br/><br/><i>I started up the stairs and then stopped. <br/>Above me on the landing stood a strange girl, about my age, with short black hair. She was smiling down at me, not a warm smile, not a friendly smil</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17717318063240893741" style="display:none">There's something off about the old house Amanda's dad inherited from a deceased uncle he's never heard of. <br /><br /><i>A cold breeze made me shiver. It was actually a beautiful, hot summer day. But the closer we got to the house, the colder I felt</i>. <br /><br /><i>Welcome to Dead House</i> offers a satisfying blend of camp and creepiness: <br /><br /><i>I started up the stairs and then stopped. <br />Above me on the landing stood a strange girl, about my age, with short black hair. She was smiling down at me, not a warm smile, not a friendly smile, but the coldest, most frightening smile I had ever seen.</i> <br /><br />And the book hints at the comedic slant R.L. Stine later brought to the series: <br /><br /><i>"Where is everyone?" I asked, looking up and down the empty street. "It's really dead around here, huh?" <br />He chuckled. "Yeah. I guess you could say that."</i> <br /><br /><i>Welcome to Dead House</i> may not be an extraordinary read for adults, but as a child this book, and the other books in the series, were irresistible and incontrovertibly spooky. They made reading fun and the act of buying a new book something to look forward to with great anticipation. </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=middle-grade-reader">middle-grade-reader</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165477508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14192544126821864035">I read this because I promised my 11 year old that I would read it with him. He hates to read anything that isn't a comic book, or at the very least, in graphic novel format. Since he loves all things creepy, I thought that this would be a great way to finally get the kid to read something with actual chapters! <br/>I think this is probably as close to perfect as it gets for a reluctant reader like my son. The chapter are short (two or three pages at the most), and yet packed with super-creepy stuff.</span>
  <span id="freeText14192544126821864035" style="display:none">I read this because I promised my 11 year old that I would read it with him. He hates to read anything that isn't a comic book, or at the very least, in graphic novel format. Since he loves all things creepy, I thought that this would be a great way to finally get the kid to read something with actual chapters! <br />I think this is probably as close to perfect as it gets for a reluctant reader like my son. The chapter are short (two or three pages at the most), and yet packed with super-creepy stuff. Nothing too graphic or gory, but still scary enough to keep a kid like mine interested. I think this book is a great introduction into the horror/paranormal genre for older children.<br /><br />I think this would probably be suitable for ages 10 and up.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11908034850004391504">I probably won't give any of these full reviews, but I grew up on the <i>Goosebumps</i> series and adored it so much that I've decided to pick it back up from the beginning. I'll probably only be reading the "main"/original series, but we'll see.<br/><br/>This was so much more fun than I remembered it being. I know I read this a few times as a kid, and read it again in my teens to find it boring, but I couldn't put it down today and had a blast revisiting Stine's writing style and his weird little ideas. It's pr</span>
  <span id="freeText11908034850004391504" style="display:none">I probably won't give any of these full reviews, but I grew up on the <i>Goosebumps</i> series and adored it so much that I've decided to pick it back up from the beginning. I'll probably only be reading the "main"/original series, but we'll see.<br /><br />This was so much more fun than I remembered it being. I know I read this a few times as a kid, and read it again in my teens to find it boring, but I couldn't put it down today and had a blast revisiting Stine's writing style and his weird little ideas. It's predictable as anything, of course, reading this as an adult (even if I didn't know for sure that I was remembering the twist correctly), but the characters are fun, the plot is quick-paced, and there's the classic "shocker" ending Stine's always been so well-known for.<br /><br />I'd be lying if I said I wasn't excited as heck to pick up book 2 soon! :P</span>

<div id="review_1294445099" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294445099" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294445099?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_kindle">ebook_kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294445099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16229803204022640023">So, my friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7091879-stepheny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stepheny</a> put it out there that she wanted to read these this summer and was all... <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433439329i/15096924.jpg' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I raised my hand. Because when I was a kid, I LOVED these books. They came out around the time I turned 10, and I was that kid who read anything and everything I could. I was the girl who WANTED reading homework. I looked forward to the Scholastic Book Fair all year long. I did the summer reading program and read circles around my classmates. By the time these books were being published, I was alread</span>
  <span id="freeText16229803204022640023" style="display:none">So, my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7091879-stepheny" rel="nofollow noopener">Stepheny</a> put it out there that she wanted to read these this summer and was all... <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433439329i/15096924.jpg" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I raised my hand. Because when I was a kid, I LOVED these books. They came out around the time I turned 10, and I was that kid who read anything and everything I could. I was the girl who WANTED reading homework. I looked forward to the Scholastic Book Fair all year long. I did the summer reading program and read circles around my classmates. By the time these books were being published, I was already reading the gamut, from Beverly Cleary to Stephen King and Dean Koontz to Little Women. If it was printed, I'd try to read that shit. <br><br>But I love horror and always have. (I remember watching Tales from the Crypt while my mom got ready to to go work at her 3rd shift security job - and I couldn't have been older than 7. Pet Sematary came out around the same time, and that shit traumatized me. The cat. And Zelda. *shudder* That freaks me out to this day!) So these books, along with the Scary Stories To Tell In The Dark, were great. They were my bus-ride-to-school reads. A little aside here: My bus driver loved listening to the radio on her route, and she loved hip-hop and R&amp;B. So I have strange associations between 90s hip-hop music and middle-grade horror stories. I can't hear the song "My Lovin'" by En Vogue without picturing this: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428089654i/14363709.jpg" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's stuck in my brain for life. <br><br>Anyway, so I read a lot of these books as a kid, and they were fun, light, nominally scary stories that were easily accessible. You never really feel like anything truly bad is going to happen because they were aimed at people of my age group (at the time) and nothing bad happens to kids. It's against the rules! It was the horror I wanted to read, but without the trauma of actual horror. It didn't keep me up at night, like Child's Play did. That fucking DOLL. Ruined dolls for me forever. <br><br>Reading this now, it's even more clear that these are innocent books geared towards kids who like to be scared but don't want to risk too much. There's an out built in to every story. This one was the house that they conveniently didn't sell yet before moving to the Mystery Uncle's estate house. So you know right then that there's little risk to the family - they can always just pick up and go home. <br><br>These books don't really hold up to much scrutiny though. I mean, for one, if a mysterious uncle left me a house that is 4 hours away, in a town I'd never heard of, I think I'd need to do a little bit more research than a single, hectic, sullen-tween-dragging walk-through. I'd need to investigate the schools and the neighborhood at a minimum, because they are supposed to actually LIVE there after they move. But right there, things would fall apart. Because there'd be nothing to investigate. There are no neighbors, and there are no teachers or students - not even a creepy lunch lady! <br><br>But OK, they do the walk-through and decide to move, because the house is paid for and they wouldn't have a mortgage anymore and dad would totally be able to dedicate his time to writing full time. Right on. Except... Why not sell the house you just got gifted, and use that money to pay off your own house, so you don't have to uproot your whole family and move to the corner of Nowhere and Nothing? Well, I mean, of course, besides the fact that there wouldn't be much of a story if they did that. <br><br>Anyway, so they pick up and move, and then things get all weird. There's ghostly footsteps and whispers in the house, and it's cold, and dreary, and "drafty". The kids, Amanda and Josh meet some weird neighborhood kids who play softball and promptly go home for lunch at 11:30am every day, and who all seem to have lived in the house that the main characters now live in. And then the dog goes missing. <br><br>Now this dog is very undoglike. I mean, it barks and runs, but if I didn't know better, I'd think that this dog was supposed to be human. They talk to it and treat it like human, which is understandable, because I talk to my cats like they are little furry humans... but my cats still act like cats - even when I anthropomorphize their behavior in my head. But this dog.. I think he thought he was human, too. It was just... not doggy enough to be real, and it was distracting and kind of obnoxious. This dog was like a precocious 4 year old child. <br><br>But anyway, Petey the dog goes missing, and the whole world collapses... and then this story takes a hard left turn from Campy Good Time Rd onto What The Hell Is Going On Blvd. The last quarter of this book RACES along, and compared to the previous 75%, which was a bit draggy and repetitive and slow, it just feels like the end is supposed to show up so suddenly that we overlook any of the stuff that it actually consists of. <br><br>The explanation for the town weirdness is literally one half of a line of dialogue. That's not counting the current reason for the family being there, which is repeated over and over... but how it all started is of the blink-and-you'll-miss-it variety. <br><br>The timeline gets incredibly wonky at the end. One minute it's "after midnight" and the kids leave the house to walk to the cemetery to find the missing dog, because they're sure it will be there. Then, after they've searched for their dog, found him, and also discovered some disturbing things in the graveyard, they run home, where they are ambushed by all the neighborhood kids. It's mentioned then that it's 2 AM, and that their parents should be home from their party (convenient) by now but they aren't and WHERE THE HELL ARE THEY? <br>Then the only other adult in the story shows up and tells the kids that they have to get out of there now, that it's dangerous, and he'll take them to their parents... so they hop in his car, and race back to the cemetery.... At which point apparently it's now daylight. Not dawn's-early-light, but full on daylight... in the course of less than an hour. <br><br>It's a strange little story, and like I said, it doesn't really hold up well under scrutiny, but for what it is, and its intended audience, it's not the worst thing I've ever read. It's quick, and light reading, so it's good for an in-between-books filler read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16229803204022640023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1727332767" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1727332767" />
    <a title="Fuzaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila"><img alt="Fuzaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532881347p2/55299343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1727332767?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuzaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuzaila" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila">Fuzaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=over-hyped">over-hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=shit-crap-and-all-things-bad">shit-crap-and-all-things-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=old-school-library-reads">old-school-library-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=goosebumps-frenzy">goosebumps-frenzy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=horror-paranormal">horror-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=i-didnt-get-the-point">i-didnt-get-the-point</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1727332767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8049929147245426488"><b>
  <i> “We killed someone who was already dead.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>There, that one sentence just about sums up how ridiculous the concept of this book is.<br/><br/>I remember the time when I first started reading, which was some four years ago. Our school library was so poorly stocked. The only books it held were the many different editions of classic books and THESE. Goosebumps books. I used to read them and love them then, but now, I don’t even want to think I used to love them once.<br/><br/> <b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br/><br/>Amanda and Josh are not at a</span>
  <span id="freeText8049929147245426488" style="display:none"><b>
  <i> “We killed someone who was already dead.”</i>
</b><br /><br />There, that one sentence just about sums up how ridiculous the concept of this book is.<br /><br />I remember the time when I first started reading, which was some four years ago. Our school library was so poorly stocked. The only books it held were the many different editions of classic books and THESE. Goosebumps books. I used to read them and love them then, but now, I don’t even want to think I used to love them once.<br /><br /> <b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br /><br />Amanda and Josh are not at all happy with their new house at Dark Falls. The town looks deserted, completely shady and eerie. But their parents insist the house is huge and cool. <br />Creepy things happen to them, and the kids in the neighborhood act strange. One extraordinarily creepy night, they find that all those friends they made, are already dead. And they want Josh and Amanda dead too.. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Thoughts</u>
</b><br /><br />- At one point, Amanda, the mc, thinks she’s more sensible and patient than her brother, BECAUSE SHE IS A GIRL<br /><br />- Sounds reasonable right? Duh. I don’t see why<b>
  <i> boys aren’t considered sensible enough?</i>
</b><br /><br />-The book was fairly readable, except, the writing was really uncool. Like, look at this –<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> “Your basketball is packed in one of these cartons,” Dad was saying. Then Josh said something. Then Dad said, “How should I know which one?” Then Josh said something. Then Dad said, “No, I don’t have time to look now. Believe it or not, your basketball isn’t at the top of my list.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />-Yeah that’s a <i>real</i> paragraph from the book. I CAN’T EVEN.. <br /><br />-Seems like R.L Stine has memorized every bit of how-to-write-a-horror-story manual. He has <b>
  <i>badly</i>
</b> used every supposedly-scary trope there is. <br /><br />* Dog barking at dead people? ✔<br />* Gross description of peeling skin and popping eyeballs? ✔<br />* Melting bodies? ✔<br />* Dead people afraid of light? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What’s a halogen light, even? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ✔<br />* Venturing to the cemetery at night and considering it ‘adventure’? ✔<br />* Century-old, nearly-dead trees? ✔<br /><br />-But what I don’t really understand is the concept. It is ridiculous to say the least. Who on earth would agree moving to a house they supposedly inherited from a non-existent great-uncle? And, dead people living in a town? They aren’t even considered as ghosts. Why are they ‘dead’ then? What does dead mean? How come, they’re not anywhere else? If they’re already dead, what happens when they ‘melt away’? Ugh, questioning the plot devices of this book is sickening.<br /><br /><br /><b>In short,</b> if you decide to overlook the questionable plot and poor writing, this book might be enjoyable. Probably.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8049929147245426488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Things get crazy in this ghostly tale of the ominous haunted house.<br/>As the first book in the series of the Goosebumps franchise, while not my favorite, I'd have to say it's still one of the great ones.</span>

<div id="review_1667813318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_940572562" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/940572562" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/940572562?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590453653" href="/book/show/1194302.Welcome_to_Dead_House">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kids interested in horror but not allowed to watch horror movies; Parents</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published1992">published1992</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=he-says">he-says</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer940572562" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18249614389149163779">Amanda and Josh didn't want to move to their new house. It's creepy - they see the faces of children in the windows and hear them whispering and giggling in their rooms. <br/><br/>Nobody can turn down a free house, though, and they inherited from their dead uncle in a stroke of luck (I'm not sure "luck" would be the word I'd use). <br/><br/>At least the kids in the neighborhood are nice. Well, except for that time they surrounded the siblings in a circle while holding baseball bats in a threatening manner.<br/><br/>And Petey</span>
  <span id="freeText18249614389149163779" style="display:none">Amanda and Josh didn't want to move to their new house. It's creepy - they see the faces of children in the windows and hear them whispering and giggling in their rooms. <br /><br />Nobody can turn down a free house, though, and they inherited from their dead uncle in a stroke of luck (I'm not sure "luck" would be the word I'd use). <br /><br />At least the kids in the neighborhood are nice. Well, except for that time they surrounded the siblings in a circle while holding baseball bats in a threatening manner.<br /><br />And Petey, the kids' sweet and friendly terrier, seems to hate everyone in town. He barks and growls at everyone, exhibiting behavior he's never shown before.<br /><br />And why is the town so dark? Yes, it is called Dark Falls, and for good reason. Trees shade every street, yard, and park. There are no streetlamps.<br /><br />It turns out that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the town is inhabited by the living dead. The town used to be a normal town, but after an accident at the plastics factory (in the '60s, I believe it's implied) a yellow mist killed everyone in town. Except they weren't dead in the traditional sense, they walk around and need "fresh blood" once a year. So every year they lure a new family to Dead House (their nickname for the only house in town where the living reside) and turn them into the living dead, too. Dogs can always sense the living dead, so they are the first to die. (Don't get too attached to Petey, is all I'm saying.) In the end, Amanda, Josh, and their parents actually escape the town unscathed after unleashing sunlight onto the undead citizens of Dark Falls. However, in the end it's revealed that they aren't killed (in a permanent sense) because the novel finishes with Mr. Dawes introducing a new family into the neighborhood.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />R.L. Stine did a great service to kids everywhere when he created a series of horror books for children. This really filled a great need. <br /><br />That being said, the books are poorly written. The writing is boring and very simple. (See my status updates for examples). Just because kids are kids doesn't mean they're stupid...kids can appreciate and deserve good writing. Also, Stine tends to end every chapter with a cliffhanger/shock-moment that 90% of the time is revealed to be nothing at the start of the next chapter. For instance, the chapter will end on "The boy crept up behind and grabbed my shoulder." Next chapter, opening sentences - it's her brother. Annoying!<br /><br />Dialogue is lame, character development is non-existent. A Goosebumps main character could be male, female, 10 or 12 - it makes no difference. Stine writes with only one voice - the kids in this series are interchangeable and forgettable. <br /><br />So why the two stars? Because Stine's creative and original horror ideas are fun and exciting. Also, he did children a great service by opening up the horror book market to them. Some of his concepts are a little silly, but most are great and really get a kid's imagination working. I always wanted someone to go back and re-write each of the original Goosebumps books in an adult form. That would be awesome and take care of the juvenile writing problem. There's a lot of potential there if Mr. Stine would agree to let an author re-write them for adults.<br /><br />I also enjoy how Stine doesn't mute the horror too much. There are some genuinely spooky moments in this book. Amanda's creepy dream about her and her family being dead and eating a meal of bones at the dining room table. The part where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Josh kills Ray with a flashlight and he turns into a skeleton and his eyeballs fall out.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The fact that every kid in the neighborhood says to the kids "I used to live in your house," when the siblings know that's not possible. And when Amanda and Josh finally <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ visit the graveyard and discover that everyone they know is dead and buried.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> These are great horror tropes, and it's fun to introduce them to kids so early. I would say that these books could be read by kids aged 8-11.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18249614389149163779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2812431532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2812431532" />
    <a title="Juli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38617426-juli"><img alt="Juli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453642808p2/38617426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2812431532?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juli" href="/user/show/38617426-juli">Juli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780590453653" href="/book/show/1194302.Welcome_to_Dead_House">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=read-openlibrary-2019">read-openlibrary-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38617426-juli?shelf=backlist-read-2019">backlist-read-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2812431532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8091365672993573544">Yep...I'm 50 years old and I'm reading Goosebumps books. Why not? The stories are fun, a bit creepy, and have a lot of nostalgia for me. Back when my oldest son was little I used to read these books out loud to him. Sometimes he would read to me. :) We did different voices for the characters and acted out the action, often ending up laughing and just having a great time. My son is now a grown man, married, and stationed in San Diego with the US Navy. This year, I promised myself I would read (or</span>
  <span id="freeText8091365672993573544" style="display:none">Yep...I'm 50 years old and I'm reading Goosebumps books. Why not? The stories are fun, a bit creepy, and have a lot of nostalgia for me. Back when my oldest son was little I used to read these books out loud to him. Sometimes he would read to me. :) We did different voices for the characters and acted out the action, often ending up laughing and just having a great time. My son is now a grown man, married, and stationed in San Diego with the US Navy. This year, I promised myself I would read (or re-read) books that I really enjoy, reviewing each one. I decided it was time to revisit the Goosebumps series just for fun, and Mom-nostalgia. <br /><br />Welcome to Dead House is the first Goosebumps book, published in 1992. At one time, my son had more than 20 of these books. We read and re-read them until he outgrew them and moved on to more in-depth stories. I did not realize how many books the Goosebumps series mushroomed into...several different spin off series....more than 100 books in total. Wow! Add in the television show and a couple movies....and the Goosebumps series really got kids reading and watching horror stories written specifically for them. <br /><br />In this first story, Josh and Amanda are upset about moving to Dark Falls. They didn't want to leave their friends behind, and the house their family inherited from an uncle is old and creepy. Little do they know just how creepy it is -- but they quickly find out! Turns out Dark Falls is hiding some dark secrets....<br /><br />Each chapter ends with a mini-cliffhanger....a bit of drama to get kids to want to read the next chapter. Perfect for silent reading, or reading out loud. The earlier books in the Goosebumps series are a bit darker and less humorous than later books. This story has some pretty gruesome and depressing imagery...but nothing graphic or too scary. Moving is often a traumatic and terrifying experience for kids. This story just turns that fear into a creepy story about a town town with dark secrets. <br /><br />The television series did a two part episode (made for TV movie) on this story. It can be streamed on Netflix for those who want to revisit some R.L. Stine goodness without reading the book. Or better yet read the book....then watch the TV version to see what changes were made. :) Welcome to Dead House is listed under Specials, episodes 11 and 12, on Netflix. <br /><br />This book made for an enjoyable afternoon's reading.....and some nice memories of time spent reading to my son. :) Dark, but entertaining and fun, story! I'm going to keep reading this series in order just for the fun of it. Great palate cleansers in-between adult fiction. :) I love children's books. There is no reason why adults can't enjoy them too! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8091365672993573544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_39973139" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39973139" />
    <a title="Nikki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1360163-nikki"><img alt="Nikki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217254879p2/1360163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39973139?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki" href="/user/show/1360163-nikki">Nikki</a>
      </span>

        rated it

  <span id="freeText8089516473171965281" style="display:none">So it’s like this. 12 year old Amanda and her 11 year old little brother Josh aren’t too thrilled about being uprooted from the house they’ve lived in their entire life just because some dead Uncle Charlie (that no one even knew anyway) left their Dad a house in his will. But here they are in Dark Falls anyway, because really, there’s only so much whining and complaining a kid can do. So like I said, now we’re at this creepy old house covered in shade trees (along with the rest of the neighborhood) and little brother Josh decides that he’d rather stay outside with Petey, the family’s pet terrier, who for some reason can’t stand to be around anyone in the entire neighborhood. Petey runs away, Josh follows, family freaks out, they all wind up in the cemetery. A foreshadow of things to come? Let's find out. A few days pass, the family gets settled in, Amanda’s been seeing children upstairs but lets everyone talk her into believing that she’s just seeing things. Josh has been having nightmares and doesn’t want to talk about it. There are whispers and billowy curtains even though the windows are closed. It’s all pretty freaky. Turns out Dark Falls is a ghost/zhombie-esque village that got destroyed after the freak “yellow-gas” incident quite a few years ago. The town doesn’t feast on brains though, so no worries there. Just fresh blood once a year.<br /><br />“I used to live in your house.”</span>

<div id="review_317341482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317341482" />
    <a title="Jory P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2032104-jory-p"><img alt="Jory P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606176929p2/2032104.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317341482?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jory P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jory P." href="/user/show/2032104-jory-p">Jory P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2032104-jory-p?shelf=teens-and-tweens">teens-and-tweens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2032104-jory-p?shelf=spooky">spooky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317341482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15482816858269681238"><i>"Where is everyone?" I asked, looking up and down the empty street. "It's really dead around here, huh?"<br/>He chuckled. "Yeah, I guess you could say that."</i> <br/><br/>TALK ABOUT FORESHADOWING. GOOD ONE, STINE. <br/><br/>I decided this year would FINALLY be my Year of Stine. I couldn't resist. I wanted to jump into the books of my young adolescent life. I've got to tell you, this is going to be super fun for me. Reading <i>Welcome To Dead House</i> was like a blast from my youth past. I used to love this book. Like a lot. It w</span>
  <span id="freeText15482816858269681238" style="display:none"><i>"Where is everyone?" I asked, looking up and down the empty street. "It's really dead around here, huh?"<br />He chuckled. "Yeah, I guess you could say that."</i> <br /><br />TALK ABOUT FORESHADOWING. GOOD ONE, STINE. <br /><br />I decided this year would FINALLY be my Year of Stine. I couldn't resist. I wanted to jump into the books of my young adolescent life. I've got to tell you, this is going to be super fun for me. Reading <i>Welcome To Dead House</i> was like a blast from my youth past. I used to love this book. Like a lot. It was always one of my favorites, now that I remember. It reminded me actually of like an <i>American Horror Story</i> but for 12-year-olds. Except its not just a house that is dead. It's the entire town. And the entire town wants Amanda and her family to join them. As the living dead of Dark Falls.<br /><br />I can see why I clearly loved these books when I was a fat, nerdy youngin' who sat on the benches of her elementary school playground reading instead of being one of the "cool kids" and swinging on the monkey bars or whatever. They are pretty engrossing. And this one grabbed my attention 100%. It always did, now that I think about it. The way Stine foreshadows the fact that everyone in the town is dead (the shaded areas, they always wear dark clothes, they cower in the sunlight...etc), is great. Its like as you are reading the stories he gives you little clues about the plotline, which I absolutely loved. My favorite had to be when they were all forced into the bright light and their faces and skin started melting off and their eyeballs fell out of their sockets. A+ imaging in my head, really. <br /><br /><i>Welcome To Dead House</i> is a good way to kick off this iconic series of spook stories for kids. The Year of Stine has begun ladies and germs, so sit back and enjoy the ride of my terrible reviews.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15482816858269681238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1421599118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421599118" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421599118?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545158886" href="/book/show/6675977-welcome-to-dead-house">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421599118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1875737856031288890">Guess what time it is, guys? Time for a walk down memory lane. It’s October so naturally I’ve been immersing myself in all things scary and one night I was reminiscing about where my love of horror began and I started thinking about revisiting Goosebumps. Well, it happened. First off, do you realize the first Goosebumps came out in 1992?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445616269i/16681942.jpg' width='399' height='225' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>No, it was not, thus making me feel officially fucking ancient I’ll tell you what. I love the idea of re-reading my childhood favorites, but what happens if its </span>
  <span id="freeText1875737856031288890" style="display:none">Guess what time it is, guys? Time for a walk down memory lane. It’s October so naturally I’ve been immersing myself in all things scary and one night I was reminiscing about where my love of horror began and I started thinking about revisiting Goosebumps. Well, it happened. First off, do you realize the first Goosebumps came out in 1992?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445616269i/16681942.jpg" width="399" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, it was not, thus making me feel officially fucking ancient I’ll tell you what. I love the idea of re-reading my childhood favorites, but what happens if its horrible? Your entire childhood becomes a lie, that’s what. But I had to take a chance, even though I took a chance on <a href="http://www.fortheloveofwords.net/book-review-party-games-fear-street-novel-r-l-stine/" rel="nofollow noopener">Stine last Ominous October</a> and it didn’t exactly pay off so instead of reading his newer stuff I decided to go back to the very beginning. And you know what? It wasn’t bad at all.<br><br><b>
  <i>“It’s really dead around here, huh?”<br>He chuckled. “Yeah. I guess you could say that.”</i>
</b><br><br>Welcome to Dead House is the very first in the original Goosebumps series (I don’t care what Amazon says trying to list this as #13 and Night of the Living Dummy as #1). It has all the makings of what scared me the most as a child and what still manages to freak me out still to this day: ghosts and things that go bump in the night. Josh and Amanda have just moved to a new town after their father received an old house from the will of a great-Uncle he never even knew existed. It’s a dark, creepy, and cold house but it’s huge and is a fantastic opportunity for their family. The kids aren’t sold. Amanda is constantly seeing things but keeps convincing herself that her mind is playing tricks on her. Her curtains move as if caught in a breeze even with the window closed and she hears footsteps in the hallway at night. But all of that is just her imagination running wild, right?<br><br>I can’t recall how long it took me to read these when I was a kid, but I ended up finishing this in a single night. It’s more of a novella for the mature reader, but it was certainly fun. While it didn’t exactly give me goosebumps because I’ve certainly read far scarier at this point in my life, it still managed to put a smile on my face taking that walk down memory lane and seeing once again what I loved so much about these when I was a kid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1875737856031288890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1567108731" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567108731" />
    <a title="Emm C²" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53296236-emm-c"><img alt="Emm C²" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558724665p2/53296236.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567108731?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emm C²" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emm C²" href="/user/show/53296236-emm-c">Emm C²</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=paranormal-supernatural">paranormal-supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53296236-emm-c?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567108731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9933700093007128571">This is the first entry and probably the best Goosebumps (right up there with Terror Tower and One Night in Horrorland). My nostalgia filter might be running a bit high when I rate it a solid five-star, but there are reasons to love it still. It's aged a lot better than some of the series, as well.<br/><br/>For one, this series, starting with <i>Dead House</i>, got so many kids into reading that wouldn't normally have. And I do mean MANY. These books were (and still are) the "In" thing for kids who love spooky s</span>
  <span id="freeText9933700093007128571" style="display:none">This is the first entry and probably the best Goosebumps (right up there with Terror Tower and One Night in Horrorland). My nostalgia filter might be running a bit high when I rate it a solid five-star, but there are reasons to love it still. It's aged a lot better than some of the series, as well.<br /><br />For one, this series, starting with <i>Dead House</i>, got so many kids into reading that wouldn't normally have. And I do mean MANY. These books were (and still are) the "In" thing for kids who love spooky stuff, or just kids who are looking for something new to read.<br /><br />For two, it's a good twist on the old haunted-house routine. And it's not <i>exactly</i> a haunted house, it's a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[town inhabited by the undead <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, which is much more interesting anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9933700093007128571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453079520" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17557237856483973582">Welcome to Dead House was the first book in the Goosebumps book series. I read it in our allotted library hours back in my elementary school. <br/>I appreciated this a lot more because this was my first goosebumps book. The story starts with Josh and Amanda moving with their parents into a relic of a house willed to them by their late uncle. Amanda and Josh felt sad about their uncle and they are not too thrilled about the new house or town. Amanda tries to give a chance on liking the new place but s</span>
  <span id="freeText17557237856483973582" style="display:none">Welcome to Dead House was the first book in the Goosebumps book series. I read it in our allotted library hours back in my elementary school. <br />I appreciated this a lot more because this was my first goosebumps book. The story starts with Josh and Amanda moving with their parents into a relic of a house willed to them by their late uncle. Amanda and Josh felt sad about their uncle and they are not too thrilled about the new house or town. Amanda tries to give a chance on liking the new place but strange things start to happen. Amanda sees and hears stuff in her room. And when their dog, Petey, goes missing, Josh and Amanda find out the town's bloody secret.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17557237856483973582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iW3UTcBshqMTqJ0BKeTT43Bfy2/LBuH3oY0p2yTk06Anit67UCWhuNpS+CgrzTkMS67jdeOnOd6RJw9z3reRHA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3qb5U7uBirFgosGqpL8UhtdKTjd3penJ/I71MXh1+gdwQfOlK8itqqlYpIOmlv5p7LtmLV8EMeDMJNOZgia4uw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2421299739511854906">Robert Lawrence Stine known as R. L. Stine and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6443810.Jovial_Bob_Stine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jovial Bob Stine</a>, is an American novelist and writer, well known for targeting younger audiences. Stine, who is often called the Stephen King of children's literature, is the author of dozens of popular horror fiction novellas, including the books in the Goosebumps, Rotten School, Mostly Ghostly, The Nightmare Room and Fear Street series.<br/><br/>R. L. Stine b</span>
  <span id="freeText2421299739511854906" style="display:none">Robert Lawrence Stine known as R. L. Stine and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6443810.Jovial_Bob_Stine" rel="nofollow noopener">Jovial Bob Stine</a>, is an American novelist and writer, well known for targeting younger audiences. Stine, who is often called the Stephen King of children's literature, is the author of dozens of popular horror fiction novellas, including the books in the Goosebumps, Rotten School, Mostly Ghostly, The Nightmare Room and Fear Street series.<br /><br />R. L. Stine began his writing career when he was nine years old, and today he has achieved the position of the bestselling children's author in history. In the early 1990s, Stine was catapulted to fame when he wrote the unprecedented, bestselling Goosebumps® series, which sold more than 250 million copies and became a worldwide multimedia phenomenon. His other major series, Fear Street, has over 80 million copies sold.<br /><br />Stine has received numerous awards of recognition, including several Nickelodeon Kids' Choice Awards and Disney Adventures Kids' Choice Awards, and he has been selected by kids as one of their favorite authors in the NEA's Read Across America program. He lives in New York, NY.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/itsthefirstdayofschoolforever/RLStine">http://us.macmillan.com/itsthefirstda...</a></span>
